<b>intap</b> <i>a</i> afraid of s.o. for his superiority. <i>Intap
kaáyu ang mga buguy níya kay ísug siya,</i>
The thugs are very much afraid of him because

<b>intáwun</b> <i>short form</i>: <b>táwun</b>. <b>1</b> particle expressing
or asking for pity. <b>1a</b> in statements.
<i>Daghan táwun ang namatay didtu,</i> A lot of
people died in that place. <i>Mu man nà táwuy
ákung panginabúhì,</i> That's what we live
from, poor us. <b>1b</b> with imperatives: please,
have mercy. <i>Iúlì intáwun nà sa labing madalì,</i>
Please return that at the earliest possible
time. <b>2</b> expressing humility: I don't necessarily
deserve s.t. good. <i>Nahinumdum táwun
siya nákù,</i> He remembers me (though I
am not important enough to be remembered).
<i>Nakadaug táwun ku,</i> I won just by luck.
<b>2a</b> with statement praising oneself, expressing
humility. <i>Kamau táwun ku ánà uy,</i> I
know how to do that. (I don't think I'm
great guns, but I do know how to do it.) <b>2b</b>
with statements that a catastrophe hasn't
happened: through the mercy of the Lord.
-----File: 0802.png--------------------------------------------------------
<i>Wà táwun mi hitabuig iltur,</i> We haven't been
hit by El Tor, thank God. <b>3</b> with a sharp denial,
taking the sting out of the denial. <i>'Anak
nu ka sa gawas ni Pidru.'--'Dílì, tawun
uy,'</i> 'They say you're Pedro's illegitimate
son.'--'Good heavens, no! (Have mercy,
don't think of that.)' <b>paN-</b> <i>v</i> [A2S; b6] say
<i>intáwun</i>. <i>Nagpangintawun siya nga nanghulam
nákù ug kwarta,</i> He kept on saying
'poor me' as he was borrowing the money.

a can in a circle and try to knock it out.

<b>-íru</b> <b>1</b> affix added to words referring to an
action not approved of to form adjectives
meaning 'one who is fond of engaging in
[such-and-such] an action'. <i>Salsalíru,</i> One
who is fond of masturbating. <i>Hambugíru,</i>
Braggart. <b>2</b> added to words referring to
things with which one can make his living
to form nouns which mean 'one who engages
in [such-and-such] an occupation'.
<i>Lab-asíru,</i> Fish vendor. <i>Labandíru,</i> Laundry-*man.

<b>irug</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [AB3; c1] @move, cause s.t. to do so.
<i>Akuy miirug sa bangkù dapit sa bungbung,</i>
I moved the chair towards the wall. <i>Nag-irug
ba nang barku sa lawud?</i> Is that ship in the
ocean moving? <i>Iruga (iirug) ug diyútay ang
sud-an ngari,</i> Move the plate of food over
here. <b>2</b> make progress, move ahead in time.
<i>Sáma lang sa wà muirug ang íyang idad,</i> She
looks as though she hasn't gotten any older.
<i>Wà giyud muirug ang ámung kahimtang,</i> Our
financial condition has made no progress. <b>3</b>
budge from one's belief. <i>Dì ni giyud siya
mairug sa íyang disisiyun,</i> He cannot be
moved from his decision. <i>n</i> progress, advancement.
<i>Gamay rag irug ang kauswágan
sa lungsud,</i> The town has undergone little
progress.

<b>iruk</b> <i>v</i> [A; a12] squeeze nits, lice on the head
with the thumbnail or perform a similar action
to relieve itching. <i>Igka giyud ang lusà
arun dì mamusà,</i> Squash the nits so they
won't hatch. <i>Igka ring katul sa ákung [=ú],</i>
Squeeze this itching spot on my head.

his own dinner. <b>sig-</b> [A13] each one [does, did]
to his own. <i>Nagsig-íyag pamaúlì ang
mga táwu dihang nag-ulan,</i> All the people
returned to their own homes when it rained.
<b>tag-</b> <i>n</i> @owner. <i>Siyay tag-íya sa sini Uryinti,</i>
He is the owner of the Oriente theater. <i>v</i>
[B1256] <b>1</b> become the owner of. <i>Ug siyay
matag-íya sa tindáhan, wà nay mupalit didtu,</i>
If he is the owner of the store, nobody
will buy there. <b>2</b> [A12] have acquired possession.
<i>Pára nakatag-íya ug usa ka taksi
garbúsu na siya kaáyu,</i> Just because she acquired
a taxi, she has become very haughty.
<b>paN-</b> <i>v</i> [A2; b5] own s.t. <i>Gastúsu kaáyu
ning ma[**à ?]nag-íya ta ug awtu,</i> It is expensive
to own a car. <b>tag-iyáhan</b> <i>a</i> having an owner.
<i>Dílì ni ikabaligyà kay tag-iyáhan na ni,</i> I
cannot sell it because s.o. owns it. <i>see also</i>
<sc>IDYAIDYA</sc>, <sc>KADAÍYA</sc>, <i>and</i> <sc>KINAÍYA</sc>.

<b>iyà</b> <i>n</i> title or term of address for women,
much older than the speaker. <i>v</i> [A; a12]
call s.o. by this title. <b>-an</b> <i>n</i> @aunt. <i>v</i> [A12; b8]

-----File: 0847.png--------------------------------------------------------
<i>musakay ug paráda,</i> My, how choosy you

<b>iyawan</b> = <sc>AWAYAN</sc>. <i>see</i> <sc>ÁWAY</sc>.

<b>iyáwat</b> for s.t. small to be of some use. <i>Díay
diyis iyáwat na lang ning ikapugung sa gútum,</i>
Here's ten cents. Perhaps this might
help stave off hunger. <i>Dì ku ibaligyà ning
yútà. Iyáwat ra ni sa ákung mga anak,</i> I
won't sell this piece of land. It will surely
be of use for my children. <i>v</i> [AN; a12]
make good use of s.t. one has little of or
can only get in limited quantities. <i>Mag-iyáwat
ka sa dáan mung sapátus,</i> Wear your
old shoes to economize. <i>Iyawáta ang ímung
panahug tuun,</i> Make good use of your limited
time by studying. <b>(->)</b> <b>1</b> = <sc>IYÁWAT</sc>. <b>2</b>
[AN; a12] do s.t. in order to save on s.t. or
get s.t. not readily available. <i>Mikúyug siya
nákù kay nangiyawat nga malibri sa plíti,</i>
He came along with me because he could
save by having me pay the fare. <i>Miapil siya
sa tím kay giiyawat ang unipurmi,</i> He joined
the team to get a free uniform.

<b>iyù</b> <i>n</i> term of address or title for a man much
older than the speaker. <i>v</i> [A; a12] call s.o.
by this title. <b>Iyù Hantuy</b> Uncle John, the imaginary
character representing the Filipino
people (s.t. like the American Uncle Sam).
<i>Gituntu si Iyù Hantuy sa mga pulitiku,</i> Politicians
are taking advantage of Uncle John.

<b>ka_{1}</b> <i>see</i> <sc>IKAW</sc>.

<b>ka_{2}</b> <b>1</b> linker between numeral and noun. <i>Tulu
ka mansánas,</i> Three apples. <i>Líbu ka líbu,</i>
Thousands and thousands. <b>2</b> between <i>isig</i> or
<i>masig</i> and nouns. <i>Ísig nímu ka táwu,</i> Your
fellow men. <i>Ang ílang masig ka áping,</i> Each
of their cheeks. <b>3</b> <b>-- ug</b> <i>particle in expressing
alternative situations</i>: 'be it ... or'. <i>Manágat</i>
-----File: 0849.png--------------------------------------------------------
<i>giyud siya mag-ulan kag mag-ínit,</i> He goes
fishing rain or shine.

<i>*ka_{3} sa -- [<i>name</i>]</i>, <b>íla -- [<i>name</i>]</b> at [name]'s
place. <i>Adtu ku sa ka Banung (íla ka Banung),</i>
I am going to Banong's place.

<b>ka_{4}</b> <i>n</i> @{letter K}.

<b>ka-_{1}</b> = <sc>NAKA-</sc>. <i>see</i> <sc>MAKA-_{1}</sc>.

<b>ka-_{2}</b> affix forming nouns which mean 'one's
-----File: 0850.png--------------------------------------------------------
co-[noun]'. <i>Ákung kaklási</i>, My classmate.
<i>Ákung katagilungsud,</i> My fellow townsman.
<i>Ákung kaáway,</i> My opponent.

<b>ka-_{3}</b> affix added to adjectives. Adjectives
plus <i>ka-</i> have these uses: <b>1</b> as nouns which
mean 'the state of being [so-and-so]'. <i>Tungud
sa ákung kasubù,</i> Because of my sorrow.
<i>Ang katahum sa palíbut,</i> The beauty
of the surroundings. <b>2</b> in exclamations. <i>Kagwápu
sa ímung balay!</i> What a beautiful
house you have! <i>Kadakù!</i> How big it is!
<b>3</b> after <i>unsa</i> to form a phrase: how (to
what extent) s.t. is [adj.]. <i>Unsa kadakù?</i>
How big is it? <i>Dì mabatbat kun unsa kangilngig,</i>
Words cannot describe how horrible
it was.

<b>ka-_{4}</b> = <sc>MAKA-_{2}</sc>.

<b>ká</b> <i>n</i> @hemorrhoids. <i>Gipaupirahan na ba níya
ang ká sa íyang lubut?</i> Did he have his hemorrhoids
operated on?

<b>káag</b> <i>v</i> [B6; c16] move in @haste. <i>Nakáag (mikáag)
siya kay mibagting na ang alas syíti,</i>
She was in a hurry because it was already
seven o'clock. <b>(->)</b> <i>a</i> doing s.t. with great
haste and carelessly. <i>Kaag kaáyu kang mamuhatbuhat.
May mga sayup,</i> You are very
fast but careless in your work. You made
lots of mistakes. <i>v</i> [B15; a12] be, become
@careless. <i>Kinsa guy musálig nímus trabáhu
nga nagkaag ka man lang?</i> Who would trust
your work when you work so carelessly?

<b>ka-an_{1}</b> inflectional affix: the local passive
potential, future. see <sc>-AN_{1}</sc>.

<b>ka-an_{2}</b> affix forming nouns <b>1</b> added to adjectives
to form nouns which mean 'the
quality of [adj.]'. <i>Kalampúsan,</i> Success. <i>Kalipáyan,</i>
Happiness. <i>Ang íyang kasuk-ánun
mauy usa ka kasukwahían sa íyang maáyung
pamatásan,</i> His quickness to anger is
not in harmony with his good manners. <b>2</b>
added to nouns or adjectives to form nouns
which refer to a group of [noun]'s. <i>Ang mga
kabatáan,</i> The children. <i>Balay sa kahiláyan,</i>
Den of vice. <i>Kanipáan,</i> Nipa swamp. <b>2a</b>
forming numbers, the multiples of ten's.
<i>Katluan</i>, Thirty. <i>Kapituan</i>, Seventy.

<b>ka-an_{3} (<-)</b> affix added to adjectives which
refer to a state to form nouns which refer
to the achievement of the state. <i>Way katin-áwan
ang inyung burúka,</i> Your case has not
reached a clear resolution. <i>Way kahusáyan
ang inyung burúka ug isig pasángil,</i> Your
case will never be resolved if all you do is
accuse each other.

<b>kabúhì</b> (from <i>búhì</i>) <i>n</i> <b>1</b> a pulsating thing located
in the abdominal region which is what
one feels when one experiences hyper-acidity
or other sharp abdominal pains. The
cause of these pains is thought to be the displacement
of the <i>kabúhì</i>, most often in an
upward direction, and treatment is by hot
compresses and by massage (<i>kalaykay</i>) to
put the <i>kabúhì</i> back in place. <i>Misáka ákung
kabúhì sa kutukutu,</i> My <i>kabúhì</i> rose to under
my rib cage. <b>2</b> this pulsating thing
viewed as the seat of life. Unsang urása nabugtù
ang íyang kabúhì? What time did he
expire (lit. was his <i>kabúhì</i> broken off)? <i>v</i>
[A13P; a4b4] have pains because of the <i>kabúhì</i>.
<i>Gikabuhían (gikabúhì) aku,</i> I have
pains in the abdominal region. <b>(->)</b> = <sc>KABÚHÌ</sc>,
<i>v</i>. <b>-un(->)</b> <i>a</i> tending to get pains caused
by <i>kabúhì</i>.

<b>kanà_{1}</b> <b>1</b> @that (near hearer, far from speaker).
<i>Mau kanay ákung gustu</i>, That is the one I
want. <b>-y bátà, láki</b> <i>expression of praise:</i> atta
boy! <i>Kanay bátà! Síging nubinta</i>, Atta
boy! You always get ninety's. <b>2</b> him, her
(referred to previously or well-known). <i>Sígi,
bisitáhan nátù nà (nà siya)</i>, All right.
Let's visit her. <b>3</b> that, this, just mentioned
or well-known. <i>Ug pagbutar kaníya ang gikinahanglan,
buhátun nátù nà</i>, If what we
have to do is vote for him, that's what we'll
do. <b>-- nga</b> when one does [so-and-so], when
[so-and-so] happens. <i>Sálum gud, kanà bang
mulanguy sa ilálum sa túbig</i>, Diving is, you
know, when you swim under water. <i>Arun
lamì ang litsun kanang ínit pa isirbi</i>, Serve
the roast pig while it is still hot so that it
will be tasty. <b>4</b> <b>-- nga ...</b> pause word used
while speaker is trying to think of what to
say. <i>Kanang, ímu úsà nga kuan, panítan</i>, Er,
you watchamacallit, you peel it first.<b>-- siya</b>
= <sc>KANÀ</sc>, <b>2</b>. <b>nà</b> short for <i>kanà</i> or <i>niánà</i>.<b>niánà</b>
<i>short form:</i> <b>ánà</b>. <b>1</b> <i>gen.:</i> of this. <i>Háin

with that? <i>Unsa may náa ánà, paríha ra

sab tung pagkaúna dà</i>, That was a good
meal. <b>2</b> food. <i>Unsay átung pagkáun dihà?</i>
What food do we have? <b>kan-un</b> <i>n</i> cooked
rice or corn. <b>kalan-un</b> <b>1</b> food. <i>Kalan-un námù
sa matag adlaw ihátag mu karung adláwa</i>,
Give us this day our daily bread. <b>2</b>
snacks. <b>-um[** space? |P3: no]-r-(->)</b> <i>a</i> ready to eat. <b>-- ug táwu</b>
be very angry. <i>Ayaw mu pagsurangsurang
kay kumakaug táwu ning ákung ginháwa</i>,
Don't provoke me because I'm so angry I
could eat s.o. right now.

<b>ka-un</b> affix added to nouns which refer to a
time of day or of life to form nouns which
mean 'period of time that it is [so-and-so].'
<i>Kagabhíun</i>, In the evening time. <i>Manunggù
ang mananagat sa sayung kabuntágun</i>, The
fishermen return in the early hours of the
morning. <i>Pribinihig kwarta ang ímung katigulangun</i>,
Set money aside for your old age.
<i>Kamatáyun</i>, @Death.

<b>ka-un(->)</b> <b>1</b> affix added to verbs which refer
to personal feelings to form adjectives which
mean 'be on the verge of, feel that one is
going to do and cannot keep himself from
it.' <i>Kahilakun kaáyu ku</i>, I was on the verge
of tears. <i>Kaihiun ku</i>, I have to urinate very
-----File: 0946.png--------------------------------------------------------
urgently. <b>1a</b> affix added to words referring
to meteorological phenomena to form adjectives
which mean [such-and-such] an
event is about to burst forth. <i>Kaulanun kaáyu
run,</i> It's just about to burst into rain
now. <b>2</b> affix added to adjectives which refer
to a state to form noun which refer to the
achievement of the state. <i>Way katagbawun,</i>
There's no satisfaction. <i>Way katapusun
ning trabahúa,</i> There's no end to this job.

in flower pots as an ornamental.

<b>kaung_3</b> <i>n</i> a sweet delicacy made from the
young fruit of the <i>buri</i> palm.

<b>kaungkuy</b> <i>n</i> old variety of white-grained paddy
rice.

<b>ka-unun(->)</b> alternant to the affix <i>ka-un(->)</i>
added to roots with a short open penult
where the vowel of the final syllable is
dropped when affixation takes place. <i>Kakataw-unun
kaáyu ku,</i> I felt very much like
laughing. <i>Way kahutdunun,</i> It never runs
out.

<b>káwas</b> <i>v</i> [AB; c] <b>1</b> get, bring out of a vehicle.

<b>kay</b> <b>1</b> @because, for the reason that. <i>Undang

-----File: 0950.png--------------------------------------------------------
<i>*yud, na hala, sígi,</i> Since you're bent on getting
married, all right, go ahead. <b>ábi --</b> just
because. <i>Ábi kay bag-ug awtu muhambug
dáyun,</i> Just because he has a new car, he
has to brag about it. <b>-- arun</b> because in
that way a desired result will happen. <i>Magtuun
ka kay arun makapasar ka,</i> You should
study so you can pass. <b>kúmu --</b> seeing as
how, because the situation is that.... <i>Kúmu
kay ikay amahan, ikay mubadlung,</i>
Since you're the father, it's your duty to
keep him in line. <i>Kúmu kay wà kuy kwarta,
dì ku magminyù,</i> Since I have no money, I
won't get married. <b>maáyu --</b> it's good that.
<i>Maáyu kay nía ka,</i> It's a good thing you're
here now. <b>tungud --</b> @because, just for the
reason that. <i>Tungud kay gikusì ka, mamúnal
diay ka?</i> Just because he pinched you,
you beat him up? <b>untà --</b> @since it is, was
like that, [so-and-so] should have happened.
<i>Untà kay ikaw may magulang, ikaw untay
dílì magpabuyag,</i> Since you are the elder,
you should have behaved yourself. <i>Untà
kay wà nay bugas, ímu untà kung giingnan,</i>
Since we were out of rice, you should have
told me. <b>2</b> @why is it that way? <i>Traynta?
Kay pabayrun ba diay ang bátà?</i> Thirty
cents? Why? You mean to say the baby has
to pay fare too? <b>--</b> [<i>interrogative</i>] Why is
it like that? Who, what, why, how, etc. is
it, that it should be like that? <i>Misulti siyag
ingun? Kay kinsa ba nà siya,</i> Is that what
he said? Why, who the hell is he? <i>Dì mau?
Kay unsa man diay tu?</i> Isn't that it? Why?
What was it then? <i>Kay ngánu man diay?
Dì ka mutrabáhu?</i> What do you mean?
You mean you don't want to work? <i>Dì
mau? Kay unsáun pa man diay?</i> What do
you mean it's not the right way? How are
we to do it then? <b>3</b> <b>--</b> [<i>dative</i>] than. <i>Dakù
siya kay kanákù (sa ákung anak),</i> He is bigger
than I am (than my child). <b>4</b> <b>-- basta</b>
<b>a</b> if [so-and-so] is done, [such-and-such] is
the result. <i>Kay basta (basta kay) ímung dugáyun
ug ínit, madáut giyud,</i> If you heat it
for a long time, it will get ruined. <b>b</b> that's
the way it is. <i>Kay basta (basta kay) mu tuy
gisulti,</i> That's the way it is. That is what he
said. <b>5</b> <b>dílì --</b> <b>a</b> it is not really that way. <i>Dílì
kay aku ray nagmulù,</i> It's not as though I
were the only one that had a complaint.
<i>Ang giingung barátu, dì kay barátu giyud,
ubus-ubus lang sa uban,</i> When he says it's
cheap, it's not really cheap. It's just a little
lower than the others. <b>b</b> not only is it [so-and-so].
<i>Dì lang kay barátu, barátu gayud,</i>
It's not just cheap, it's very, very cheap. <b>dílì
-- ... kun dílì</b> not only ... but also. <i>Dì lang</i>

<b>kayhà</b> (usually pronounced <i>kahà</i>) <b>1</b> @perhaps,
@possibly. <i>Kayhà mahikalimut pa usab siya
kang Mirilin kun mahigugma siya sa láin,</i>
Perhaps he will forget Marilyn again if he
falls in love with s.o. else. <b>1a</b> <b>kayhà ... kayhà</b>
maybe because ... or perhaps because.
<i>Nanghátag siya--kahà kay manggihatágun,
kahà kay dihay giapas,</i> He gave me s.t.,
maybe to be nice or maybe he was after
s.t. <b>2</b> in questions <b>a</b> with no interrogative:
by any chance, I wonder if. <i>Muanhi ba kahà
siya?</i> Will he come by any chance? <i>Dílì siya
makahúbad, aku pa kahà?</i> Even he can't
translate it. Could I possibly do so? <b>b</b> with
an interrogative: who (what, where, etc.)
can it be? <i>Ginúu ku, unsa kahay nahitabù?</i>
My Lord! What can have happened? <i>Unsáun
ku kahà pagbáyad sa útang?</i> How
could I ever pay the debt? <b>c</b> maybe, approximately.
<i>Magkinahanglan kahà kug tulu,</i>
I'll need approximately three. <b>3</b> <b>man --</b>
since apparently [so-and-so] is the case.
<i>Mutan-aw ka man kahà sa sini. Ngánung nía[** typo?]
ka pa man?</i> You said you were going to the
movies. Why are you still here? <b>-an(->)</b> <i>a</i>
s.t. held doubtful or uncertain. <i>'Makapasar
kahà siya sa iksámin?'--'Kayhaan pa,'</i>
'Will he pass the examination?'--'It is still
doubtful.' <i>'Anus-a ka magpakasal níya?'--'Sa
kayhaan,'</i> 'When will you marry her?'--'Someday
(but when, I still do not
know).' <b>2</b> accidentally, unexpectedly. <i>Sa
kayhaan nagkítà sila sa Manílà,</i> By chance
they met in Manila.

<b>kinhud</b> = <i>KIHUD</i>.

<b>kini_{1}</b> short forms: <b>ni, king</b> <b>1</b> @this (near speaker
and person spoken to). <i>Pila man ni?</i> How
much is this? <b>1a</b> <b>mau -g --</b> expression used
in lieu of giving reasons or excuses why s.o.
failed to do s.t. or cannot do s.t. <i>Mau kinig
kini, mau kanag kanà.... Sus, daghan kaáyug
katarúngan,</i> Because of this and this,
and that and that ... there's no end to reasons
why he couldn't do it. <b>1b</b> this one
now. <i>Tinúud na karun kining ákù,</i> What I
am saying now is true. <b>2</b> this well-known
kind of. <i>Natural, kay láin man ning kumbira
ug walay bayli ug ínum!</i> Of course! Because
a (lit. this) party is no good without
dancing or drinking. <b>3</b> he, she (person just
referred to). <i>Átù ning tabangan,</i> Let's gang
up on him. <b>4</b> <b>-- nga</b> pause word used when
one is hesitant about plunging into things.
<i>Kining, nía ku kay dúna kuy ihangyù,</i> Err, I
came here because I have a request. <b>4a</b> this
action of, when one does. <i>Uh, unsa gud
ning ámut na pud!</i> What's all this stuff

<b>kinsa</b> <b>1</b> @who, @whose? <i>Kinsay muanhi rung

-----File: 0973.png--------------------------------------------------------
<i>Kinsa ring lapis?</i> Whose pencil is this? <i>--
[noun]-a</i> <b>2</b> which person (of several). <i>Kinsang
batáang naligsan?</i> Which child was it
that was run over? <b>3</b> <i>in phrases:</i> <b>bísan --</b>
anybody, and everybody. <i>Ang mayur nag-awhag
kang bísan kinsa nga ang sidula pagabayran
giyud,</i> The Mayor urges anyone and

one at all, no matter who it is. <i>Way si (ni)
bísan kinsa ang makahilabut niíni,</i> No one,
and I don't care who, can touch this. <b>kang
--</b> whose. <i>Kang kinsa ni?</i> Who does this belong
to? <b>-- pa a</b> who else? <i>Kinsa pay gustung

who in the world! <i>Kinsa pay layhan nga
mutrabáhu ug mau nay swildu!</i> Who in the

the salary! <b>-y ngálan</b> <i>[gen.]</i> what is [gen.]'s
name? <i>Kinsay ngálan níya?</i> What is his
name? <b>si -- a1</b> s.o. who thinks he's of importance
but is not. <i>in interrogative sentences:</i>
who does he (she) think he is? <i>Si kinsa
ba siyang musúgù nákù?</i> Who is he to command
me? <b>a2 mu rag si --</b> as if he were s.o.
<i>Nagpasugùsúgù si Ambuy mu rag si kinsa,</i>
Amboy is giving orders as if he were s.o. <b>a3
abi, kaingun</b> <i>[gen.]</i> <b>ug si --</b> [gen.] thought
it was s.o. of importance, when it wasn't.
<i>Ingun nákù ug si kinsa, ikaw diay,</i> For a
moment I thought it was s.o., but it was
just you. <b>b -- kadtung</b> whoever, anyone
who. <i>Si kinsa tung makapildi sa higanti hatágag
primyu,</i> Whoever can kill the giant
gets a reward. <b>kinsáun, maha-, mahakinsakinsa</b>
whoever it turns out to be. <i>Bísan kinsáun
(mahakinsa, mahakinsakinsa) padayunun
sa balay,</i> Whoever comes, she just lets
him come into the house. <b>kinsakinsa</b> anybody
and everybody. <i>Kinsakinsa na lang
duktur ákung gitawag. Wà ma maáyu ang

<b>kinta_1, kintà_1, kint[va]</b> <b>1</b> let's just consider how
it would be--perhaps it is so, perhaps not.
<i>Naghátag sila arun kinta pagpakítà sa kadaghánan,</i>
They gave some perhaps just for appearances'
sake (or perhaps in all honesty).
<b>1a</b> supposing that it is or will be the case.
<i>Kinta nagtúu kang kináwat ku kadtu. Unsay
pagtúu mu kanákù--kawatan?</i> Supposing
you think I stole it. What do you think I
am, a thief? <i>Kinta ig-adtu ku didtu, bayran
na ku nímu?</i> Let's say I go there. Will you
pay me? <i>Kinta bungatan kag dyís, hangyúag
dus,</i> If he offers to sell it for, say, ten, offer
two for it. <b>1b</b> let's say for the sake of
the game or the story. <i>Ang nakakuhag dyís
puntus, kinta, muy mananáug,</i> The one
who gets, say, ten points wins. <i>Ang gilay-un
sa ílang balay gíkan sa ámù, ingun kinta dinhi
ug ngadtu sa Kapitulyu,</i> Their house was
about as far from ours as, say, it is from
here to the Capitol. <b>2</b> pretending to be. <i>Naghilak
kinta ka, ayaw paila nga nagkumidiya,</i>
You're supposed to be crying. Don't let on
you're joking. <b>2a</b> since [so-and-so] is, after
all, the case. <i>Ikaw man kintay pinyalan dinhi--ayúha
pagdá ning ímung mga sákup,</i>
You're supposed to be in charge here, so
treat your men fairly. <b>3</b> <b>kay --</b> why, is [so-and-so]
really the case (when it shouldn't
be)? <i>Kay kinta ikaw bay magbuut dinhi?</i>
Why, do you think you have the right to
have the say here? <i>Kay kinta siya ra giyuy
taypist--mangítà tag láin,</i> What the hell.
Does he think he's the only typist in the
world? We'll look for another one. <i>Kay
kinta patrabahúun pa giyud kug maduminggu?</i>
What? Do I have to work on Sundays,
too? <b>kintáhay</b> = <sc>KINTA_1,</sc> <i>1, 2.</i>

<b>kubransa</b> <i>v</i> [A; b(1)] make a collection of a

manggátus káda adlaw</i>, I collect almost a
hundred pesos daily. <i>n</i> <b>1</b> action of collect-*
-----File: 0999.png--------------------------------------------------------
*ing. <b>2</b> amount collected or bill presented.

<b>kubri_{1} = KUBLI.</b>

<b>kubri_{2}</b> <i>n</i> k.o. simple kerosene lamp made of
a flat bottomed metal cup with a spout
having a wick on it.

<b>kubri_{3}</b> <i>v</i> [A; b6(1)] cover one's obligation
or what is lacking. <i>Dúnay nagkubri sa ákung
amutan kay wà man ku paningli</i>, S.o. paid
for my obligation because nobody collected
from me.

<b>kubrikáma</b> <i>n</i> bedspread, bed cover. <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A; b]
put a bedspread on a bed. <b>2</b> [a12] make
into a bedspread.

<b>kubu = KUBA.</b>

<b>kubù</b> <i>a</i> stoop-shouldered. <i>Ságad sa mga tisísun
kubù</i>, Most people with TB are stoop-shouldered.
<i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A; c1] stoop a little, bend
over. <i>Nikubù siya pag-ági sa mabang pultahan</i>,
He stooped when he went through the
low door. <b>2</b> [B] for the posture to be
hunched over.

<b>kubul</b> <i>v</i> [B2] <b>1</b> for s.t. cooked to come out
tough or hardened. <i>Mukubul ang pánit sa
giasal kun dì humdan ug túbig</i>, The roast
pig skin becomes tough if it has been roasted
without daubing water on it. <i>Nagkakubul
na ang kindi nga ákung gilútù</i>, The candy
I'm cooking is gradually hardening. <b>2</b>
become hardened, insensitive. <i>Mikubul (nakubul)
na ang íyang kasingkásing sa tanang
biaybíay</i>, Her feelings have become hardened
to any and all insults. <i>Nagkakubul ang
ákung láwas sa katugnaw</i>, My body is gradually
becoming inured to the cold. <i>a</i> <b>1</b> hardened.
<b>2</b> hardened in feelings, insensitive.
<i>Kubul siya sa mga pakilúuy</i>, She is insensitive
to pleas for mercy. <b>kublan</b> <i>a</i> <b>1</b> invulnerable.
<i>Dì nà siya dutlan ug bála kay kublan</i>,
Bullets can't pierce him because he is invincible.
<b>2 = KUBUL</b>, <b>a. v</b> [B] become invulnerable.

<b>kubung_{1}</b> <i>n</i> drinking glass made of a piece of
bamboo some 5" long cut just below a
node which serves as the bottom. <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A1; c16]
make into such a bamboo glass. <b>2</b> [A13; c1][**joined A1 & 3]
use or put s.t. in such a bamboo glass.

<b>kubung_{2}</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> protective covering. <b>2</b> mosquito
net. <i>v</i> [A1; b6] put up a protective covering,
make into a protective covering. <i>Gikubungan
sa mananagat ang lampara arun dì
mapálung</i>, The fisherman put a covering
over the lamp to keep the wind from blowing
it.

<b>kubung_{3} = KÚLUT.</b>

<b>kúbung</b> <i>n</i> keyhole limpets, limpets with a
small hole at the top of the shell, living in
shallow water.

<b>kubus</b> <b>a</b> low in amount. <i>Kubus ang bili sa is-*</i>
-----File: 1000.png--------------------------------------------------------
<i>*mágul</i>, Smuggled goods are cheap. <i>v</i> [AB2; b7c]
for an amount to become less, cause
it to do so. <i>Mukubus ang swildu ug hínay
ang nigusyu</i>, Salaries go down when business
is poor. <i>Kubsan ang ímung tagal sa pagbáyad
sa útang</i>, We'll shorten the term for
you to pay off the debt.

<b>kubut</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [AC; b(1)] hold, take hold of s.t.
<i>Kinsay nagkubut sa lyábi?</i> Who has the
key? <i>Magkúbut ta arun dì ta magkabúwag</i>,
We'll hold hands so that we won't be separated. [**f1: bold looks like scan error]
<i>Nawálà ang lápis nga ákung gikubtan</i>,
The pencil I was holding got lost. <b>1a</b> [AN; b6(1)N]
hold on to s.t. to keep from falling.
<i>Nangubut (mikubut) siya nákù kay
danglug</i>, He held on to me because it was
slippery. <b>1b</b> [A3; b8] get hold of s.t. to
have it. <i>Wà pa ku makakubut ánang kantidára</i>,
I had not held such an amount (of
money). <i>Hikubtan sa pulis ang kawatan nga
miiskápu</i>, The policeman happened to get
hold of the thief who was about to escape.
<b>1c</b> [A2] hold on by sticking to it. <i>Ang
iskats tip mukubut kaáyu sa átung papitlan
niíni</i>, Scotch tape adheres well to whatever
you stick it to. <b>2</b> [A; b(1)] occupy, hold a
certain position or office. <i>Ang katungdanan
nga íyang gikubtan</i>, The position he is holding.
<b>3</b> [A; b26] handle, play, operate. <i>Maáyu
siyang mukubut sa sista</i>, She plays the
guitar well. <i>Sipii ang nagkubut sa íyang libru
sa tindáhan</i>, A CPA takes care of the
accounts in their store. <b>4</b> [A; b(1)] keep a
mistress. <i>Dúna siyay gikubtan nga hustis</i>,
He has a night club hostess for a mistress.
<b>(<-)</b> <i>v</i> [A; a12] wed s.o. on his deathbed by
just having the couple hold hands and blessing
them. <i>Kadaghan na makakúbut ang párì
ug himatyung páris nga nabúhì</i>, The priest
has officiated at many deathbed weddings
where the dying partner recovered. <b>kubtanan</b>
<i>n</i> handle. <b>kinubtánan</b> <i>n</i> keepsake among
close friends or sweethearts.

<b>kubútan = KULABÚTAN.</b>

<b>kubyirta</b> <i>n</i> covered decks of ships.

<b>kubyirtus</b> <i>n</i> silverware. <i>v</i> [A1; c] use silverware.
<i>Magkubyirtus mig mangáun kun adúnay
bisíta</i>, We use silverware when we have
visitors. <b>paN-</b> v [A; b] put silverware on the
table.

<b>kúd</b> <i>n</i> code, secret writing. <i>v</i> [A13] write in
code.

<b>k[=ú]d = KÚLUD.</b>

kudakan nang byúha</i>, That is a good
view to take a picture of. <b>pa-</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A; b]
have one's picture taken. <i>Nagpakudak ang
bag-ung kasal</i>, The newly weds had their pic-*
